    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="review_233372535" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/233372535" />
    <a title="Nathalie Brault" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4662622-nathalie-brault"><img alt="Nathalie Brault" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474723299p2/4662622.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/233372535?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathalie Brault" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathalie Brault" href="/user/show/4662622-nathalie-brault">Nathalie Brault</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer233372535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1768604021632028566">I've just finished reading a totally different type of book that I'm used to reading.<br/>And I must say that I enjoyed it.<br/><br/>This is a fiction-mystery genre book.<br/><br/>When loyalty to his bike club and his brothers has been Damage's life and route to wealth, what happens when business becomes serious and brother starts killing brother?<br/><br/>Heavy Duty People is the story of a biker which is quite well written by author/journalist Iain Park and Martin Robertson who's nickname in the book is Damage.<br/><br/>The story takes p</span>
  <span id="freeText1768604021632028566" style="display:none">I've just finished reading a totally different type of book that I'm used to reading.<br />And I must say that I enjoyed it.<br /><br />This is a fiction-mystery genre book.<br /><br />When loyalty to his bike club and his brothers has been Damage's life and route to wealth, what happens when business becomes serious and brother starts killing brother?<br /><br />Heavy Duty People is the story of a biker which is quite well written by author/journalist Iain Park and Martin Robertson who's nickname in the book is Damage.<br /><br />The story takes place in the UK. It's the story of Damage's journey, from when he was a teenager, joining a charter, known to us here as a chapter and growing with them as a biker. This club is an independent one known as The Legion. This club is all about brothers being loyal to one another. Across the rest of the world, the biker's gang wars are raging and it starts to echo into the UK. And so one day the president of the The Brethren called Dazza, the top charter of the UK, makes an offer to The Legion to join them. Because smaller charters across the UK are joining bigger ones if not there are wars. And so The Legion guys are fused into The Brethren except for those who don't want to , those have their patches removed. <br />But Dazza is driven by power and money more then loyalty. Nothing will stand in his way to get it, not even murder. So when her gets Damage's 3 best buddies killed, Damage swears he will get revenge. He then plans his revenge with some of his brothers that had their patches removed.<br />SO when the time comes, Damage and his brothers take over Dazza and his goons and he becomes the new President of The Brethren.<br /><br />From what I understand and what I read, the writer must rider a bike also. Because, the way he describes the bikes and the way they ride in the book gave me the impression of actually being on a bike.<br />It was awesome. I could almost sense the wind in my hair. <br />Riding must be a passion for him.<br /><br />I give this book 4 stars.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1768604021632028566" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_460603797" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/460603797" />
    <a title="Andy Hornsby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14790177-andy-hornsby"><img alt="Andy Hornsby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353506389p2/14790177.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/460603797?book_show_action=true">Nov 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andy Hornsby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andy Hornsby" href="/user/show/14790177-andy-hornsby">Andy Hornsby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer460603797" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8276871379134911800">Taking as its backdrop the life of a normal bloke in a fictitious back patch club based in the North East of England, Heavy Duty People is a natural successor to those New English Library books that provided the inspiration to many a British biker and possibly the perfect book for those who – like myself – can only speculate as to what goes on behind closed doors at clubhouses across the country. I considered passing it to one who’d know but Amanda has started reading it now, so it won’t be goin</span>
  <span id="freeText8276871379134911800" style="display:none">Taking as its backdrop the life of a normal bloke in a fictitious back patch club based in the North East of England, Heavy Duty People is a natural successor to those New English Library books that provided the inspiration to many a British biker and possibly the perfect book for those who – like myself – can only speculate as to what goes on behind closed doors at clubhouses across the country. I considered passing it to one who’d know but Amanda has started reading it now, so it won’t be going anywhere for a while.<br /><br />Nicely written, I desperately tried to pick holes in the research, which is so often the downfall of books written outside an author’s personal experience, but Parke describes himself as a biker and that comes across in the way he deals with the riding elements. <br /><br />I took it as read that the shared writing credit given to Martin Robertson reflected the assistance of an insider to keep the club business real, which proved to be the case after a fashion, and the blurring of the lines between fact and fiction works very well, but there’s a part of you that wonders how the first person perspective works out ... but all becomes clear in the end.<br /><br />I couldn’t help but wonder how a member of a real patch club would see it, but then I thought back to the episodes of ‘The Sons of Anarchy’ that I forced myself to sit through, just so’s I’d know why I didn’t want to sit through it again, and the responses of club members – varying from enthusiasm to apathy, but no outright hostility – and that reduced this tale to a good story, well told, bringing out a real empathy for the central character, the oft-quoted Damage, and the dilemmas he faces. <br /><br />A real page turner as it reaches its climax, with an unexpected twist that’s worth the wait.<br /><br />As published in American-V #41</span>
  <a data-text-id="8276871379134911800" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4664321496855402076" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this read - a memoir style account told from the perspective of 'Damage', a man who when unsure where he was going with his life, became a member of a motorcycle clube and found it gave him a sense of purpose and belonging which had previously been missing.<br />Damage tells us how the small independent and democratic club he belonged to, changes direction after a takeover by a larger club - The Brethren, which had a different way of working.<br /><br />Superbly written, Damage tells us of the crime, violence and dealings that went on and how he managed to cleverly manipulate people and situations to reverse things to work out more in his favour.<br /><br />I initially thought this was a biography rather than fiction and, without spoiling the twist at the end which put a different slant on things, I am still not entirely sure. This book is very interesting, well-written, refreshing and an original, enjoyable read - a wonderful inside glimpse into the closed world of the motorbike groups.<br />I am looking forward to reading the other books in this series.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3612598106" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15286627356789516988">This book, the novel takes place inside a fictional British motorcycle gang. From the very beginning just the feel of the book from the description of the characters, the countryside, and the narrator of the story you have the sense of being told the story as someone who is in the gang or club as an informant not as a member. The dark way it is told adds to the story and really shows how the club and Damage the person telling the story will go through in the choices that need to be made. Will it</span>
  <span id="freeText15286627356789516988" style="display:none">This book, the novel takes place inside a fictional British motorcycle gang. From the very beginning just the feel of the book from the description of the characters, the countryside, and the narrator of the story you have the sense of being told the story as someone who is in the gang or club as an informant not as a member. The dark way it is told adds to the story and really shows how the club and Damage the person telling the story will go through in the choices that need to be made. Will it be worth it all of the club decisions? Does Damage follow the club because he has to or does he find the strength to leave and be with his love? There also will be another book this one though is a very good story, with good characters and makes you feel like you are there with them. I received this book from Netgalley.com I gave it 5 stars. Follow us at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.1rad-readerreviews.com">www.1rad-readerreviews.com</a></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17796174-kristi-cramer?shelf=alpha-males">alpha-males</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer847272365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8561508505874404845"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/>I was given this book free through Story Cartel in exchange for a review. I eventually liked this story, but it took until almost the end before I decided that. It was rather flat, and there wasn't much action until about half, maybe 2/3 of the way through. I never really considered abandoning it, but I kept waiting for all the excitement. When it finally arrived, it was abrupt and surprising. I think the surprise was what redeemed the story. Maybe. I mean, I'm on the fence about it, be</span>
  <span id="freeText8561508505874404845" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br />I was given this book free through Story Cartel in exchange for a review. I eventually liked this story, but it took until almost the end before I decided that. It was rather flat, and there wasn't much action until about half, maybe 2/3 of the way through. I never really considered abandoning it, but I kept waiting for all the excitement. When it finally arrived, it was abrupt and surprising. I think the surprise was what redeemed the story. Maybe. I mean, I'm on the fence about it, because all through the story I didn't get the sense that things were going to play out the way they eventually did. I bought it, but only just. (Can't go into detail without offering spoilers.)<br /><br />I didn't feel much connection with Damage, other than really kind of liking his morals. Of course that went straight to hell by the end of the book....<br /><br />Another factor that may have really affected my enjoyment of the story is that the formatting was crap. I don't know if it was my download, or if they are all that way, but it looked like poetry instead of a novel. The text would go for a line and a half, then skip a line and go for another line and a half, regardless of punctuation or paragraph endings. It may be that my need to increase the font size had a distorting effect, but an eBook should be able to flow to whatever size the reader needs. There were also plenty of spelling errors, and not just the difference between the Queen's English and American English. Heavy Duty People could use a heavy duty proofreading. If I hadn't been so distracted by the formatting, I may have been able to squeeze another half star out of this. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8561508505874404845" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText18432841964254485414" style="display:none">If your going to read this book, "Pack a teddy. A fucking big one. you know. like the ones they have at the fair. Hold on fucking tight.....It gonna be a ride alright. <br /><br />This book was the real deal and I liked it. No it was not filled with love and sex and all the girlish fantasy's that most MC books have come down to recently. This book was more true to the real life MC. A scary world filled with violence, drugs, betrayal, power, respect and choices. <br /><br />At first I was not getting into this book it until, I started getting into Damage the main character's head. He was kind of a poet a philosopher a thinker, <br /><br />"with pride in the colors came an addiction to respect. It was all about belonging". All these MC's wanted respect and to belong to something bigger than themselves. <br /><br />Don't we all want to belong to something bigger than ourselves? That is what Damage wanted. <br /><br />You know people like to think they're so clean. But really they're all dirty in some way or other. I suppose part of the difference is just that the MC's don't try and pretend otherwise. <br /><br />So, Im sure to most people this is more like a man's book. But I ended up really liking it a lot. Not to say that a little more about the wife and the things a girl wants to read about may have gave it a larger audience with the girls. I ended up really enjoying Damage and his thoughts and quotes....</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer5112644077402069387">Reviewed on behalf of 2 Girls Who Love Books Blog<br/>I am not a quitter. I just want to state that in the beginning, because this book made me be one. It was so boring and exhausting to read that I couldn’t get over about 25 %. I gave up. There is so much telling telling telling and nothing happens.   <span id="freeText5112644077402069387" style="display:none">Reviewed on behalf of 2 Girls Who Love Books Blog<br />I am not a quitter. I just want to state that in the beginning, because this book made me be one. It was so boring and exhausting to read that I couldn’t get over about 25 %. I gave up. There is so much telling telling telling and nothing happens. It is more like the main character was writing his biography and even for that it was boring. I have read a few biographies from people who were in MCs. Dangerous, real MCs where the handling was better than this book. <br />I just couldn’t get into it, since not even the writing style was worth to push myself through pages over pages of boring telling what is happening. Like I said I was about 25 % into the book and still I had no idea what would happen after the meeting that took place in the beginning. <br />There are few authors that I tolerate for being more telling than showing (on some parts in the book) that is because these authors invented a whole new world they had to explain, but this author put his story in the real world and just couldn’t come to a point. <br />I’m sorry, but I can only give one star for this book since I expected something more exciting from the blurb. Sorry.<br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11686003401803425646">Wow, um ok so at the beginning of this book I was a bit overwhelmed. There is a lot of Motorcycle clubs mentioned, merging and joining, plus their territories and the boundaries for each that are located in a part of the world I know nothing about, so needless to say it was confusing.   <span id="freeText11686003401803425646" style="display:none">Wow, um ok so at the beginning of this book I was a bit overwhelmed. There is a lot of Motorcycle clubs mentioned, merging and joining, plus their territories and the boundaries for each that are located in a part of the world I know nothing about, so needless to say it was confusing. But I did my best and pushed through because hey I’m a sucker for an MC story. This was unlike any MC story I have read. It is not sexy or romantic, its raw and gritty. This story reads like a diary. In the back of the book, the author says it is the story of the man as told to the author, but then the last paragraph states that it is a work of fiction, so that leaves me, again, confused. Regardless if it is work of fiction or based on a true story, it is a very intriguing story. I enjoyed it immensely and look forward to reading more work by this author. I give this book 4 stars. </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('/s8dtLvgcQVzI3lPJO7ZFksu3FMkx2cYjYmZJODb+7y/Ll7Vh6WH54wXBd1FqsXT+RXP/QcDoSAUnzl8UX9n3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PCULm8/mchCYnFCnQnuB6pq2fwlAuKExhLgeX7D0EW59xEj686OE8meoLDUjP50vKI1sp2N8Zwkdrr4HAVCNDw==')})
  }

a call to SignInPromptController#get to determine if the user should see the sign in interstial.

last seen the insterstitial.  If the controller responds indicating the popup should appear, the
React component will render its content.
-->
